\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_ReadBootHoldReason()}{DLPC654X\_ReadBootHoldReason()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Read\+Boot\+Hold\+Reason (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint8\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Reason\+Code }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Returns the code that specifies the reason for being in bootloader mode.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em Reason\+Code} & Reason code~\newline
0x00 BOOT\+\_\+\+HOLD jumper in HOLD position ~\newline
 0x01 Switched to programming mode initated by main app ~\newline
 0x02 Reading flash info failed ~\newline
 0x03 Flash layout mismatch ~\newline
 0x04 Can\textquotesingle{}t initialize ARM peripherals ~\newline
 0x05 Can\textquotesingle{}t allocate memory pool ~\newline
 0x06 Failure in initialization task ~\newline
 0x07 Error in USB init ~\newline
 0x08 Error in i2c init ~\newline
 0x09 Error getting app configuration ~\newline
 0x0A App configuration layout mismatch ~\newline
\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_ReadChecksum()}{DLPC654X\_ReadChecksum()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Read\+Checksum (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{Start\+Address,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{Num\+Bytes,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Simple\+Checksum,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Sumof\+Sum\+Checksum }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command computes and returns the checksum starting at the given address for the specified number of bytes. Checksum is calculated as below\+:-\/ ~\newline
 uint32 Simple\+Checksum = 0; ~\newline
 uint32 Sumof\+Sum\+Checksum = 0; ~\newline
 uint08 $\ast$\+Addr = (uint08 $\ast$) Start\+Address; ~\newline
 ~\newline
 while (Num\+Bytes--) ~\newline
 \{ ~\newline
 Simple\+Checksum += $\ast$\+Addr++; ~\newline
 Sumof\+Sum\+Checksum += Simple\+Checksum; ~\newline
 \} ~\newline



\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Start\+Address} & Start Address offset for checksum computation where Offset 0 refers to first byte in the flash, 1 refers to second byte and so on. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Num\+Bytes} & Number of bytes to compute checksum \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em Simple\+Checksum} & Simple additive checksum \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em Sumof\+Sum\+Checksum} & Sum of simple additive checksum calculated at each address\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Read\+Db\+Aperture\+Min\+Max (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint16\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Apt\+Min,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Apt\+Max }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command gets the minimum and maximum aperture positions. The minimum command typically corresponds to the aperture position for the aperture to be fully closed, while the maximum command typically corresponds to the aperture position for the aperture to be fully open. However, the polarity of these may change depending on the aperture hardware used.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_af59efbc74773b07ca079023fb32f7dc7}\label{dlpc654x_8c_af59efbc74773b07ca079023fb32f7dc7}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_ReadDbHistogram@{DLPC654X\_ReadDbHistogram}}
\index{DLPC654X\_ReadDbHistogram@{DLPC654X\_ReadDbHistogram}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_ReadDbHistogram()}{DLPC654X\_ReadDbHistogram()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Read\+Db\+Histogram (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint8\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Hist\+Ptr }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command returns the start address of the Dynamic\+Black(tm) II (DB) histogram data. The histogram contains scene brightness data from the previous frame. The DB histogram contains 34 bins measuring non-\/overlapping intensity ranges in the displayed image. The value of each bin equals the number of pixels within the bin\textquotesingle{}s intensity range. Each pixel\textquotesingle{}s intensity is calculated as the maximum of its red, green, and blue values. In other words, pixel intensity = MAX( R, G, B ). Each pixel has a format of unsigned 8.\+8, making 16 bit values. Bins 32 and 33 are special bins that represent pixels that have values of exactly zero and only fractional values respectively. This function can be used independently of aperture control for image improvement in dark scenes.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em Hist\+Ptr} & Start address of the DB histogram array. Array size is 34. The LSB of each bin represents 32 pixels. Each bin saturates at 0x0003\+FFFF.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_a95ba0054ab87d80b7847e2facbd4f218}\label{dlpc654x_8c_a95ba0054ab87d80b7847e2facbd4f218}}

This command enables the Dynamic\+Black(tm) II Manual Mode of operation. It is intended to be used as a test command. The DB software algorithm will be disabled, and the user can set manual gain values using DB set gain command.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_afd11651986fc41b3edc01fc90d6e4c48}\label{dlpc654x_8c_afd11651986fc41b3edc01fc90d6e4c48}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_ReadFlashWrite@{DLPC654X\_ReadFlashWrite}}
\index{DLPC654X\_ReadFlashWrite@{DLPC654X\_ReadFlashWrite}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_ReadFlashWrite()}{DLPC654X\_ReadFlashWrite()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Read\+Flash\+Write (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Num\+Bytes\+To\+Read,  }\item[{uint8\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Data }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command is used to read data from flash. This command shall be called only after setting the start address and size using the \mbox{[}\mbox{[}\#t-\/initialize\+\_\+flash\+\_\+read\+\_\+write\+\_\+settings\+\_\+write\mbox{]}\mbox{]} command. ~\newline
 Flash\+Read commands can be chained till the initialized number of bytes are returned. The bootloader will auto-\/increment the address and size for each command. Only the initialized number of bytes will be returned. Calling the function after returning requested data will return in command failure. This command supports variable sized response.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Num\+Bytes\+To\+Read} & Num bytes to read in this command \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ out}}  & {\em Data} & The bytes read from the flash\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

This command sets up the user defined 3x3 warping map that shall override the keystone correction, anamorphic scaling and other warping feature settings. a 3x3 warp map table given by the parameter of this command is used but creates a smooth warping output by interpolating the intermediate points. To disable this feature use Configure\+Warp\+Map command.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteDbApertureMinMax()}{DLPC654X\_WriteDbApertureMinMax()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Db\+Aperture\+Min\+Max (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Apt\+Min,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Apt\+Max }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command controls the minimum and maximum aperture positions. The minimum command typically corresponds to the aperture position for the aperture to be fully closed, while the maximum command typically corresponds to the aperture position for the aperture to be fully open. However, the polarity of these may change depending on the aperture hardware used.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Apt\+Min} & Position where the aperture is fully open or closed (depending on aperture hardware polarity). Range = 0 to (Composer configured minimum), and must be less than Apt\+\_\+\+Max. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Apt\+Max} & Position where the aperture is fully open or closed (depending on aperture hardware polarity). Range = 0 to (Composer configured maximum), and must be greater than Apt\+\_\+\+Min.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

This command controls how far open or closed the aperture should be over the light source. The aperture position is adjusted every frame based on the current scene brightness. Note\+: This function should only be used during calibration and only when the Dynamic\+Black(tm) II algorithm is disabled.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_acf3f807c4026d556c376e5bcb9640944}\label{dlpc654x_8c_acf3f807c4026d556c376e5bcb9640944}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteDbBorderConfiguration@{DLPC654X\_WriteDbBorderConfiguration}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteDbBorderConfiguration@{DLPC654X\_WriteDbBorderConfiguration}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteDbBorderConfiguration()}{DLPC654X\_WriteDbBorderConfiguration()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Db\+Border\+Configuration (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Top,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Bottom,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Left,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Right }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command configures area of the Dynamic\+Black(tm) II border region for the border exclusion function. The border exclusion function allows the user to reduce the letterbox (black border) effect on a primarily bright image where letterbox area reduces the overall scene brightness for the algorithm. It also helps the algorithm better handle images with bright subtitles where the subtitles increase the overall scene brightness. This command will also be used in a multi-\/\+ASIC configuration to exclude any image overlap required for other image processing algorithms.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Top} & number of lines top of border. Range 0 -\/ 4095 \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Bottom} & number of lines bottom of border. Range 0 -\/ 4095 \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Left} & number of pixels of left border. Range 0 -\/ 2047 \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Right} & number of pixels of right border. Range 0 -\/ 2047\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteDbStrength()}{DLPC654X\_WriteDbStrength()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Db\+Strength (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{Strength }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This function controls the Dynamic\+Black(tm) II strength. A higher strength value will cause Dynamic\+Black(tm) II to be more aggressive in closing the aperture for a given scene brightness. The aperture min and max positions have to be set prior to calling this function. The aperture movement strength range is 0 to 3, with a recommended value of 2.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Strength} & Aperture movement strength setting. Range = 0 to 3, with a recommended value of 2.\\

\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteDisplayImageSize@{DLPC654X\_WriteDisplayImageSize}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteDisplayImageSize@{DLPC654X\_WriteDisplayImageSize}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteDisplayImageSize()}{DLPC654X\_WriteDisplayImageSize()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Display\+Image\+Size (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_d_l_p_c654_x___display_image_size__s}{DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Display\+Image\+Size\+\_\+s}} $\ast$}]{Display\+Image\+Size }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Configures the cropping of input image and resizing of image that is displayed. Cropped area can be equal to or less than the input image size. The display area has has to be within DMD effective number of pixels and lines. Note\+: -\/ sending this command would override the settings made through Set Aspect Ratio command. ~\newline
 -\/ For TPG, SFG and Splash, cropped\+Area parameter is ignored. For those sources, cropped area is automatically set as explained below\+: ~\newline
 -\/ For TPG, cropped area is set to TPG resolution. ~\newline
 -\/ For Splash, cropped area is set to Splash image size. ~\newline
 -\/ For SFG, cropped area is set to SFG resolution which is equal to source area of last stable external source or TPG. ~\newline

\end{DoxyParams}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteEepromLockState()}{DLPC654X\_WriteEepromLockState()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Eeprom\+Lock\+State (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{Lock\+State }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets the lock state of EEPROM. When lock is set, all writes to EEPROM settings and/or calibration data from application software will not be actually written to the EEPROM. The locked mode is to be used only in factory where user wants to play around with various settings without actually recording them in the EEPROM. In normal use mode, the lock is not supposed to be set.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Lock\+State} & \textquotesingle{}0\textquotesingle{} -\/ Unlocked~\newline
\textquotesingle{}1\textquotesingle{} -\/ Locked\\

\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteEepromMemory@{DLPC654X\_WriteEepromMemory}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteEepromMemory()}{DLPC654X\_WriteEepromMemory()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Eeprom\+Memory (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Index,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Size,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{Pwd,  }\item[{uint8\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Data }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Writes data to EEPROM connected to the controller. ~\newline
 The EEPROM holds settings and calibration data. The primary purpose of this function is for the user to write to areas of EEPROM outside of the settings and calibration data. If user wants to overwrite settings/calibration data, the password sent with the command should match the expected password. This is a protection mechanism to prevent accidental overwrite of settings/calibration data.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Index} & Index of the memory to write to (0 means first byte in EEPROM, 1 means second byte and so on) \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Size} & Number of bytes to be written \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Pwd} & EEPROM password if the user needs to write to the TI specified memory space \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Data} & Data\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_a027b18b3fe45f2f8ee69949b629ac66b}\label{dlpc654x_8c_a027b18b3fe45f2f8ee69949b629ac66b}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteEraseSector@{DLPC654X\_WriteEraseSector}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteEraseSector@{DLPC654X\_WriteEraseSector}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteEraseSector()}{DLPC654X\_WriteEraseSector()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Erase\+Sector (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{Sector\+Address }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command erases the sector of the flash where the given address falls in. This command is a flash update command, and requires flash operations to be unlocked using \mbox{[}\mbox{[}\#t-\/unlock\+\_\+flash\+\_\+for\+\_\+update\+\_\+write\mbox{]}\mbox{]} command. The sector address shall be specified as an offset from flash start address. For example in a flash device where all sectors are 64KB of size, sector addresses shall be specified as follows\+:-\/ ~\newline
 Sector 0 = 0 ~\newline
 Sector 1 = 0x10000 ~\newline
 Sector 2 = 0x20000 ~\newline
 and so on... ~\newline



\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Sector\+Address} & Sector Address ~\newline
\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_a1f772621048470584f5783692697beb9}\label{dlpc654x_8c_a1f772621048470584f5783692697beb9}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteFlashWrite@{DLPC654X\_WriteFlashWrite}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteFlashWrite@{DLPC654X\_WriteFlashWrite}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteFlashWrite()}{DLPC654X\_WriteFlashWrite()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Flash\+Write (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Data\+Length,  }\item[{uint8\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Data }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command is used to program data to flash. This command shall be called only after setting the start address and size using the \mbox{[}\mbox{[}\#t-\/initialize\+\_\+flash\+\_\+read\+\_\+write\+\_\+settings\+\_\+write\mbox{]}\mbox{]} command. This command is a flash update command, and requires flash operations to be unlocked using \mbox{[}\mbox{[}\#t-\/unlock\+\_\+flash\+\_\+for\+\_\+update\+\_\+write\mbox{]}\mbox{]} command. ~\newline
 Flash\+Write commands can be chained till the initialized number of bytes are programmed. The bootloader will auto-\/increment the address and size for each command. Only the initialized number of bytes will be programmed even if more data is provided. ~\newline
 {\bfseries{It is important to send only even number of bytes per flash write command to ensure all bytes are written. This is done so that all flash writes are optimized as per the multi-\/word write supported by the flash device.}} This command supports variable sized payload.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Data\+Length} & Byte Length for Data \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Data} & Data to write to flash memory\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteHdrSourceConfiguration()}{DLPC654X\_WriteHdrSourceConfiguration()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Hdr\+Source\+Configuration (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_d_l_p_c654_x___hdr_source_configuration__s}{DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Hdr\+Source\+Configuration\+\_\+s}} $\ast$}]{Hdr\+Source\+Configuration }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

HDR maps wider brightness and color range of HDR sources to projector brightness and color range. The mapping requires multiple source groups and system groups define the HDR source and projection device properties respectively. This command sets the source properties and based on this information nearest source group is selected for mapping.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteIlluminationEnable()}{DLPC654X\_WriteIlluminationEnable()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Illumination\+Enable (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{Enable }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Enables the illumination system. In color wheel based lamp or laser systems, the illumination will be turned on only if the system has indicated that the color wheel is spinning. This interlock is necessary to avoid burning the coatings off the glass, but is less of an issue with printed wheels.

 4 -\/ Only Blue LED Enabled ~\newline
 5 -\/ Red and Blue LEDs Enabled ~\newline
 6 -\/ Green and Blue LEDs Enabled ~\newline
 7 -\/ All LEDs Enabled ~\newline

\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_aa64651f72e508ea2e1b8bebe50e75c74}\label{dlpc654x_8c_aa64651f72e508ea2e1b8bebe50e75c74}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteImageAlgorithmEnable@{DLPC654X\_WriteImageAlgorithmEnable}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteImageAlgorithmEnable@{DLPC654X\_WriteImageAlgorithmEnable}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteImageAlgorithmEnable()}{DLPC654X\_WriteImageAlgorithmEnable()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Image\+Algorithm\+Enable (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_d_l_p_c654_x___image_algorithm_enable__s}{DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Image\+Algorithm\+Enable\+\_\+s}} $\ast$}]{Image\+Algorithm\+Enable }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets enable flag for all Image Algorithms.~\newline
 0 = Disable ~\newline
 1 = Enable ~\newline
 {\bfseries{Chroma Transient Improvement}} \+: ~\newline
 This function enables/disables the Chroma Transient Improvement (CTI) function which filters the 4\+:4\+:4 sampled, chrominance (Cr and Cb) data on the B and C data channels. The chroma transient functions performs band pass filtering (supports two center frequencies) and median filtering for ringing minimization. It performs limiting and coring functions for the filtered output. ~\newline
 {\bfseries{Gamma Correction}} \+: ~\newline
 This function enables/disables the Gamma Correction function which implements the removal of gamma transfer function applied at the source, via table lookup process called de-\/gamma. When enabled, perform de-\/gamma translation of the 10-\/bit RGB input to the common 12-\/bit floating point (S0\+M8\+E4) RGB output. When disabled, the full 10 bits of each data input to the Gamma Correction function are zero padded and MSB-\/aligned to 12-\/bits and passed through unmodified.~\newline
 {\bfseries{Color Coordinate Adjustment}} \+: ~\newline
 This function enables/disables the Spatially Adaptive Seven Primaries Color Correction Function Enable. When Disable forces 3x3 CSC (Color Space Conversion) with identity. ~\newline
 {\bfseries{Brilliant Color}} \+: ~\newline
 This function enables/disables the Brilliant\+Color technology, Brilliant Color uses up to five colors, instead of just the three primary colors, red, green and blue, to improve color accuracy and brightens of secondary colors. This results in a new level of color performance that increases the brightness of the colors. ~\newline
 {\bfseries{White Point Correction}} \+: ~\newline
 This function enables/disables the White Point Correction, typically used on LED type illumination systems. Sometimes due to increase in LED operating temperature or LED aging the LEDs output wavelentgh drifts, therefore white point of the system shifts. This algorithm using active light sensor feedback and factory calibrated values help maintaing white point of the system. ~\newline
 {\bfseries{Dynamic Black}} \+: ~\newline
 Dynamic Black (DB) is an algorithm that reduces the amount of light reaching the projection path by means of LED output power through current control and compensates for reduced light by gaining up the RGB signals. ~\newline
 {\bfseries{HDR}} \+: ~\newline
 High Dynamic Range (HDR) is an algorithm that maps wider brightness and color range of HDR source to the projector display range. HDR is affected by several factors such as illimuniation characterstics, duty cycle distribution and current running sequence. A valid HDR source should be set by HDR\+\_\+\+Set\+Hdr\+Source\+Configuration() before enabling HDR processing.~\newline



\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Image\+Algorithm\+Enable} & ~\newline
\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteImageBrightness@{DLPC654X\_WriteImageBrightness}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteImageBrightness@{DLPC654X\_WriteImageBrightness}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteImageBrightness()}{DLPC654X\_WriteImageBrightness()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Image\+Brightness (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{Brightness\+Adjustment }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

The brightness control provides the ability to add or subtract a fixed bias from each of the input channels. This may be used to remove any inherent offsets and/or adjust the brightness level. The brightness coefficients are signed, 11-\/bit (s8.\+2), 2\textquotesingle{}s complement values between -\/256 and 255.\+75, inclusive. Brightness Control is used after color space conversion.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Image\+Gamma\+Curve\+Shift (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int8\+\_\+t}]{Red\+Shift,  }\item[{int8\+\_\+t}]{Green\+Shift,  }\item[{int8\+\_\+t}]{Blue\+Shift,  }\item[{int8\+\_\+t}]{All\+Color\+Shift }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Used to specify the shifts in the gamma curve of Red, Green and Blue. A left shift is a positive offset and a right shift is a negative offset. The effective brightness is increased with a left shift and decreased with a right shift.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteImageRgbGain()}{DLPC654X\_WriteImageRgbGain()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Image\+Rgb\+Gain (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Red\+Gain,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Green\+Gain,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Blue\+Gain }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Adjusts individual R, G and B gains of the source image. Gain is specified as a percentage from 0\% -\/ 200\%, with 100\% being nominal (no gain change). 0\% will zero out the channel. This function adjusts R, G and B gains by altering the Color Space Converter (CSC) coefficients. This function is only applicable to RGB sources.

\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteImageSharpness@{DLPC654X\_WriteImageSharpness}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteImageSharpness@{DLPC654X\_WriteImageSharpness}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteImageSharpness()}{DLPC654X\_WriteImageSharpness()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Image\+Sharpness (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{Sharpness }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Configures the sharpness filter. A value of 0 is the least sharp (most smooth), while a value of 31 is the most sharp. This filter is in the back end of the data path, so both video and graphics are affected. TI recommends that the sharpness filters be disabled (sharpness=16) for graphics sources.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Sharpness} & Sharpness value to apply.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

This command initializes flash read/write operation. This command shall be called before a \mbox{[}\mbox{[}\#t-\/flash\+\_\+write\+\_\+command\mbox{]}\mbox{]} command is sent. Note\+: For Flash Write, the Address and download size set up shall both be even.\+\_\+\+\_\+

This Command Initializes the on the fly splash load operation. It is used to give the information about the image (dimensions, pixel format, compression used and so on) and sets the datapath for the splash load operation. It also resets prior operations. It should be called once before loading an image on the fly.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_a8573a1276f6d3fb51843c0b4dc945413}\label{dlpc654x_8c_a8573a1276f6d3fb51843c0b4dc945413}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteKeystoneAngles@{DLPC654X\_WriteKeystoneAngles}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteKeystoneAngles()}{DLPC654X\_WriteKeystoneAngles()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Keystone\+Angles (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{Pitch,  }\item[{double}]{Yaw,  }\item[{double}]{Roll }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Configures the Keystone correction when the pitch, yaw, roll, throw ratio and vertical offset of corrected image are known. Keystone correction is used to remove the distortion caused when the projector is not orthogonal to the projection surface (screen). Keystone feature will be automatically enabled when this command is executed.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Pitch} & Pitch angle in degrees \\
\hline

 Set to 0 for 1D correction \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Roll} & Roll angle in degrees ~\newline
 Set to 0 for 1D/2D correction\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_a12f412b44d95bd273a81d6c8c2baaacd}\label{dlpc654x_8c_a12f412b44d95bd273a81d6c8c2baaacd}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteLoadSplashImageOnTheFly@{DLPC654X\_WriteLoadSplashImageOnTheFly}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteLoadSplashImageOnTheFly@{DLPC654X\_WriteLoadSplashImageOnTheFly}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteLoadSplashImageOnTheFly()}{DLPC654X\_WriteLoadSplashImageOnTheFly()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Load\+Splash\+Image\+On\+The\+Fly (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Image\+Data\+Length,  }\item[{uint8\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{Image\+Data }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This Command receives the image data and writes it into the VPS DRAM Buffer. It performs decompression if required. Due to the limitation of USB, the entire image data may not be sent in one go. Hence, this command has to be called multiple times in order to load the entire image. It also stores any bytes that are unprocessed by the API (if the API does not have all the bytes required to perform an operation). These unprocessed bytes are sent over to callback function the next time data is received. The API displays the loaded splash once the entire image is loaded into the memory. The remaining pixels to load the image is also returned by the callback function.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Image\+Data\+Length} & Byte Length for Image\+Data \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Image\+Data} & Image Data\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_a006c8539f14fea822b7a6856ded4cd1c}\label{dlpc654x_8c_a006c8539f14fea822b7a6856ded4cd1c}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteManualWarpControlPoints@{DLPC654X\_WriteManualWarpControlPoints}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteManualWarpControlPoints@{DLPC654X\_WriteManualWarpControlPoints}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteManualWarpControlPoints()}{DLPC654X\_WriteManualWarpControlPoints()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Manual\+Warp\+Control\+Points (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Horizontal\+Ctrl\+Points\+Length,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Vertical\+Ctrl\+Points\+Length,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_d_l_p_c654_x___manual_warp_control_points__s}{DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Manual\+Warp\+Control\+Points\+\_\+s}} $\ast$}]{Manual\+Warp\+Control\+Points }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command sets up the user defined control points of the warp map that shall be applied on top of the keystone correction, anamorphic scaling and other warp dependent feature settings if they are enabled. The warping map table loaded by the \mbox{[}\mbox{[}\#t-\/manual\+\_\+warp\+\_\+table\+\_\+write\mbox{]}\mbox{]} command is used as a two dimensional array with dimension which is defined based on the argument Are\+Control\+Points\+Evenly\+Spaced of this command\+: -\/ TRUE = (Warp\+Columns x Warp\+Rows) -\/ FALSE = (WRP\+\_\+\+CTL\+\_\+\+POINTS\+\_\+X x WRP\+\_\+\+CTL\+\_\+\+POINTS\+\_\+Y) The points in the map should lie within the display area defined by \mbox{[}\mbox{[}\#t-\/disp\+\_\+image\+\_\+size\+\_\+command\mbox{]}\mbox{]}. Any points lying outside the display area shall get cropped.


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}

\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Vertical\+Ctrl\+Points\+Length} & Byte Length for Vertical\+Ctrl\+Points \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Manual\+Warp\+Control\+Points} & ~\newline
\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Ti\+Act\+Query\+Type} & Query type ~\newline
0 = Query N number of bytes from offset address provided in next two bytes i.\+e., Bytes 1-\/2 ~\newline
 1 = Query Actuator information also print on UART debug port ~\newline
 2 = Query AWG Data Set for index number provided in next two bytes i.\+e., Bytes 1-\/2~\newline
 3 = Query AWG Edge table header for index number in next two bytes i.\+e., Bytes 1-\/2~\newline
 \\
\hline

{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Tpg\+Predefined\+Pattern (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{Pattern\+Number }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command will set one of the pre-\/defined test patterns stored in flash (configured using DLP Composer tool). The function selects a pattern to load from flash into the test pattern generator hardware. The information retrieved from the flash includes pattern definition, color definition, and the resolution. The pre-\/defined patterns are included in the flash configuration data. \mbox{[}\mbox{[}\#t-\/display\+\_\+write\mbox{]}\mbox{]} command must be called to switch the display mode from other modes to TPG prior to or after this command .

{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Unlock\+Flash\+For\+Update (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{dlpc654x_8h_aa88d3ef61e59e29996d0b9ea57089cab}{DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Cmd\+Flash\+Update\+T\+\_\+e}}}]{Unlock }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command unlocks the flash update operation (Download, Erase). By default the flash update operations are locked. This is to prevent accidental modification of flash contents. To unlock, the pre-\/defined key shall be send as the unlock code. Calling this command with any other parameter will lock the flash update commands.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_ac8d41ed5a8e4cd21bbe15f43059d1ae1}\label{dlpc654x_8c_ac8d41ed5a8e4cd21bbe15f43059d1ae1}}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{dlpc654x_8c_aa7f584238454a5065954732a10933713}\label{dlpc654x_8c_aa7f584238454a5065954732a10933713}} 
\index{dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}!DLPC654X\_WriteXprActuatorWaveformControlParameter@{DLPC654X\_WriteXprActuatorWaveformControlParameter}}
\index{DLPC654X\_WriteXprActuatorWaveformControlParameter@{DLPC654X\_WriteXprActuatorWaveformControlParameter}!dlpc654x.c@{dlpc654x.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DLPC654X\_WriteXprActuatorWaveformControlParameter()}{DLPC654X\_WriteXprActuatorWaveformControlParameter()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Xpr\+Actuator\+Waveform\+Control\+Parameter (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{dlpc654x_8h_ad9c8fa7f3d61f2e286bb52c719b1e4f0}{DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Xpr4\+Way\+Command\+\_\+e}}}]{Xpr\+Command,  }\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{Awc\+Channel,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{Data }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This command configure/setup Actuator Waveform Control(\+AWC) block. Here, AWCx can be AWC 0 or 1. Bytes 2-\/5 contains the XPR command data as mentioned in Byte 0. While Byte 1 contains AWC channel to be confifure, possible value are 0 or 1.~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Fixed Output Enable}} \+: Configures Actuator in fixed output mode.~\newline
 Byte 2\+: 0x00 -\/ Disable 0x01 -\/ Enable ~\newline
 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{DAC Gain}} \+: Set Waveform Generator DAC Gain.~\newline
 Byte 2\+: Range 0 -\/ 255 format u1.\+7 (0 to 1.\+9921875) ~\newline
 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Subframe delay}} \+: Subframe delay Bytes 2-\/5; Range 0 -\/ 262144 and lsb = 133.\+333ns ~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Actuator Type (READ ONLY)}} \+: Actuator type ~\newline
 Byte 2\+: ~\newline
0x00 -\/ NONE ~\newline
 0x01 -\/ Optotune (XPR-\/25 Model) ~\newline
 0x80 -\/ TI Actuator Interface (EEPROM) ~\newline
 0x81 -\/ TI Actuator Interface (MCU) ~\newline
 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Output Enable/\+Disable}} \+: Actuator output enable/disable ~\newline
 Byte 2\+: 0x00 -\/ Disable 0x01 -\/ Enable ~\newline
 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline
 Note\+: Both AWC0 and AWC1 disabled/enabled together ~\newline
 {\bfseries{Clock Width}} \+: Defines the high and low width for the output clock; the clock period will be 2$\ast$(Clk\+Width+1)$\ast$8.33ns~\newline
 Bytes 2-\/5 \+: Clk\+Width ~\newline
 Example\+: Clk\+Width = 0; will generate clock of 2$\ast$(0+1)$\ast$8.33 = 16.\+66ns ~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{DAC Offset}} \+: DAC Output Offset ~\newline
 Byte 2\+: Range -\/128 -\/ +127 format S7 (-\/128 to +127) ~\newline
 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Number of Segments}} \+: Defines number of segments ~\newline
 Byte 2\+: Range 2 -\/ 255~\newline
 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Segments Length}} \+: Defines size of the segments ~\newline
 Bytes 2-\/3\+: Range 19 -\/ 4095~\newline
 Bytes 4-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x0000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Invert PWM A}} \+: Applicable when AWC is configured to PWM type instead of DAC ~\newline
 Byte 2\+: 0x00 -\/ No inversion ~\newline
 0x01 -\/ Inverted ~\newline
 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Invert PWM B}} \+: Applicable when AWC is configured to PWM type instead of DAC ~\newline
 Byte 2\+: 0x00 -\/ No inversion 0x01 -\/ Inverted ~\newline
 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Subframe Filter Value}} \+: Sets Subframe Filter Value -\/ defines the minimum time between Subframe edges. Edges closer than the set value will be filtered out ~\newline
 Byte 2\+: 0 = Filter disabled, \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}0 = Filter time will be Val x 60us, Range\+: 0 -\/ 255 ~\newline
 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Subframe Watch Dog}} \+: Defines the maximum time between Subframe edges; if timer expires, then the WG will automatically output the Fixed Output value, and the normal output will resume on the next subframe edge.~\newline
 Bytes 2-\/3\+: 0 = Subframe watchdog disabled, \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}0 = Watchdog time will be Time x 60us, Range\+: Range\+: 0 -\/ 1023 ~\newline
 Bytes 4-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x0000~\newline
~\newline
 {\bfseries{Fixed Output Value}} \+: Defines the value to be output on DAC when fixed output mode is selected.~\newline
 Byte 2\+: Value to be output on DAC, Range -\/128 to 127 Bytes 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000~\newline
~\newline



\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Xpr\+Command} & XPR Command \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Awc\+Channel} & Channel number (0 or 1) of Actuator waveform control for which the command parameter has to be applied \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Data} & Data that needs to be passed to the command\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
0 if successful, error code otherwise 
\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Xpr\+Subframe\+Filter\+Value (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{Channel\+Num,  }\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{Subframe\+Filter\+Value }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

{\bfseries{Subframe Filter Value}} \+: Sets Subframe Filter Value -\/ defines the minimum time between Subframe edges. Edges closer than the set value will be filtered out. -\/-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} Byte 2\+: 0 = Filter disabled, \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}0 = Filter time will be Val x 60us, Range\+: 0 -\/ 255 -\/-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} Byte 3-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x000000

{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t DLPC654\+X\+\_\+\+Write\+Xpr\+Subframe\+Watch\+Dog (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{Channel\+Num,  }\item[{uint16\+\_\+t}]{Subframe\+Watch\+Dog }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

{\bfseries{Subframe Watch Dog}} \+: Defines the maximum time between Subframe edges; if timer expires, then the WG will automatically output the Fixed Output value. and the normal output will resume on the next subframe edge. -\/-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} Bytes 2-\/3\+: 0 = Subframe watchdog disabled, \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}0 = Watchdog time will be Time x 60us, Range\+: Range\+: 0 -\/ 1023 -\/-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} Bytes 4-\/5\+: Reserved must be set to 0x0000
